% Dataset Collection: Colonial Era Weather Archive
% Type: TMAX - Monthly
% Version: LATEST
% Dataset Hash: d4007075d4018cc53e3edc08ca9a3e6a
% 
% ------------------------------------
% 
% This file is a plain text export of a portion of the temperature data contained 
% in Berkeley Earth Surface Temperature Analysis.
% 
% The associated dataset name is shown above, while this file should have the 
% name
% 
% 	site_complete_detail.txt
% 
% For general information about this data product, please refer to the data set 
% readme file: README.txt
% 
% The current file is the "site_complete_detail" export, which contains a 
% detailed summary of the stations appearing in this dataset.  Information is 
% presented in tab delimited columnar format.  Primary temperature data, 
% secondary data such as quality control flags, and other metadata can be found 
% in other files in the same directory and should be distributed together.
% 
% In addition, the files:
% 
% 	site_summary.txt
% 	site_detail.txt
% 
% Provide alternative ways to access information regarding each site and may be 
% used in place of this file.  The current file is meant as an exhaustive 
% accounting of the information about each station, and may be more detailed than 
% is necessary for many uses.  For synthesis information please refer to 
% site_detail.txt.
% 
% For each site presented here, there are a number of location reports.  Each 
% location report comes from a specific source and in many cases they reflect a 
% specific time interval during which the associated location metadata is 
% supposed to be valid.  In this way changes in station location and identity can 
% be described through time.
% 
% The columns contained in this file are as follows:
% 
% 	Station ID: A unique integer identifying each station
% 
% 	Report Number: An index to the metadata report.
% 
% 	Station Name: The station name used in the report.
% 
% 	Country: The country that the station was located in at that time.  In some 
% cases non-sovereign territories are designated when they are geographically 
% isolated from their parent country.  For example, the Carribean island of 
% Martinique, administered by France, is designated as "Martinique [France]".  
% The code "[Missing]" is used if the country is not known.
% 
% 	Record Start Date: Specifies the earliest time for which the report is 
% expected to apply.  If the earliest time is unknown, a value of -9999 is used.
% 
% 	Record End Date: Specifies the most recent time for which the report is 
% expected to apply.  If the most recent time is unknown, a value of -9999 is 
% used.
% 
% 	Source: The name of the source from which the metadata record was taken.
% 
% 	Latitude: The latitude of the station in degrees and decimal fraction of a 
% degree.  Latitudes run from -90 to +90, where negative numbers indicate 
% positions in the southern hemisphere.  Missing values are reported as -999.
% 
% 	Longitude: The longitude of the station in degrees and decimal fraction of a 
% degree.  Longitudes run from -180 to +180, where negative numbers indicate 
% positions in the western hemisphere.  Missing values are reported as -999.
% 
% 	Elevation: The reported elevation of the station in meters above mean sea 
% level.  Missing values are reported as -999.
% 
% 	Alternate Elevation: The reported alternative elevation of the station in 
% meters above mean sea level as reported by the source.  The nature of the 
% alternative elevation report varies by source.  A typical example might be a 
% third party map reference elevation for the stated latitude and longitude.  
% Missing values are reported as -999.
% 
% 	Latitude Uncertainty: The estimated uncertainty on the reported latitude.  
% Where possible this is based on appropriate metadata; however, in many cases it 
% is simply a reflection of the precision with which the latitude was reported.  
% Undetermined values are reported as -9.999.
% 
% 	Longitude Uncertainty: The estimated uncertainty on the reported longitude.  
% Where possible this is based on appropriate metadata; however, in many cases it 
% is simply a reflection of the precision with which the longitude was reported.  
% Undetermined values are reported as -9.999.
% 
% 	Elevation Uncertainty: The estimated uncertainty on the station elevation.  
% Where possible this is based on appropriate metadata; however, in many cases it 
% is simply a reflection of the precision with which the elevation was reported.  
% Undetermined values are reported as -9.999.
% 
% 	Relocations Flag: A flag whose values is "1" if the issuing agency explicitly 
% declared that this report represents a relocation of the temperature station.  
% Value is "0" otherwise.
% 
% 	State / Province Code: A code indicating the state, province, or similar 
% political subdivision of the designated country that the station is located in. 
% In most cases these use two letter codes and reflect conventional designations 
% within the designated country.  Missing and unspecified values are blank.  
% 
% 	County: The name of the county, or similar political subdivision, that the 
% station is located in.  This field is usually blank except for some stations in 
% the United States.
% 
% 	Time Zone: The UTC offset of local standard time at the location of the 
% station, if known.  A value of -99 is used to indicate missing values.
% 
% 	WMO ID: The World Meteorological Organization identification number assigned 
% to the station, if any.  Stations which do not have or fail to report a WMO ID 
% are assigned a value of -9999.  
% 
% 	Coop ID: Identification number assigned as part of the United States 
% Cooperative Observer Network.  The first two digits are specific to the state 
% or territory the station resides in.  Missing values are assigned value -9999.
% 
% 	WBAN ID: The Weather Bureau / Army / Navy identification number assigned to 
% the station, if any.  Missing values reported as -9999.
% 
% 	ICAO ID: The International Civil Aviation Organization identification code.  
% This is a four letter code usually only assigned to airports.  Missing values 
% are left blank.  
% 
% 	USAF ID: The USAF identification code.  This is a six digit code where the 
% first five digits are often the same as the WMO ID.  Sites that are also WMO 
% stations will typically have "0" for the final digit.  Missing values are 
% assigned value -9999.
% 
% 	NCDC ID: Eight digit identifier code used in the National Climate Data Center 
% Multi-Network Metadata System.  Missing values are assigned value -9999.
% 
% 	Instrument Type: Kind of instrument used.  This field is currently unused but 
% is reserved for future use.
% 
% 	Other Ids: String used to encode other id codes used for this station.  Such 
% ids are often specific to the originating database.
% 
% 	Archive Key: This string is a unique alphanumeric identifier used by Berkeley 
% Earth to identify the originating dataset and entry for this report.
% 
% 	Hash: A 128-bit MD5 hash expressed as a hexadecimal string.  This hash is 
% derived from the record's metadata, and hence uniquely identifies the record.  
% The intended use of this field is as an aid to help identify changes in station 
% metadata.
% 
% 
% 
% Comments regarding metadata merging:
% 
% The process of identifying when the station reported in one data set is the 
% same as the station reported in another data set is complex and relies on 
% comparisons of data and metadata.  Full details will be presented elsewhere; 
% however, some overview comments are provided here to help the user understand 
% this data.
% 
% The process of merging data from different sources is largely automated and is 
% believed to be efficient, but it is not perfect.  There will be cases where two 
% records should have been recognized as the same site, but weren't recognized as 
% the same.  Similarly, there will be some cases where a merge occured 
% erroneously.  It is believed that error rate from both types of problems is 
% small, though it has not yet been fully quantified.
% 
% Temperature station site records are intended to be associated with a single 
% station having a fixed location.  However, historical observers have at times 
% relocated stations even while continuing to use the same station names and ID 
% codes.  Such relocation events are known to introduce discontinuities in 
% temperature records that advanced users of this data set may need to be aware 
% of and investigate.  Information of station moves can be gained from this file 
% and is further summarized in the "station_changes.txt" file.
% 
% A further confounding factor is that historical datasets have in some cases 
% combined data from distinct stations together in order to form longer synthetic 
% records.  These combination records may then have been further copied and 
% combined without clear documentation of the fact that they represent data from 
% several different stations.  As one begins to unwind such combinations it is 
% not unusual to find that the data is associated with multiple identifiers (such 
% as WMO or COOP ID codes) that in principle ought to be unique.  Similarly 
% confounding, there have been a number of occurrences where WMO and other codes 
% have been reassigned or reused.
% 
% An extreme example of such historical merging has occured with "Washington 
% National Airport", where composite records were formed by combining data from 
% the airports now known as "Washington Dulles" and "Washington Reagan" with 
% historical records from "Hoover Field" and "Bolling Field".  This occured even 
% though these distinct airports are separated by up to 20 miles.  It is 
% difficult at this point to unwind which data values originally came from each 
% site.  At the moment, data that was merged together in upstream data sets will 
% generally remain merged in our data product.  Reviewing this data file can help 
% to identify examples of such merging.  When multiple records across disperse 
% locations have been combined, the summary data in "site_detail.txt" will assign 
% a large uncertainty to latitude and longitude sufficient to encompass the 
% multiple locations used.
% 
% Users of this dataset who wish to understand the history of individual sites 
% are encouraged to review the data in this file to help begin to reach that 
% understanding.  Though many weather stations have uncomplicated histories, a 
% few have had very complicated histories indeed.
% 
% 
% ------------------------------------
% Station ID, Report Number, Station Name, Country, Record Start Date, Record End Date, Source, Latitude, Longitude, Elevation (m), Alternative Elevation (m), Lat. Uncertainty, Long. Uncertainty, Elev. Uncertainty (m), Relocation Flag, State / Province Code, County, Time Zone, WMO ID, Coop ID, WBAN ID, ICAO ID, USAF ID, NCDC ID, Instrument Type, Other IDs, Archive Key, Hash
